GT Equivalence Verification (BPG5)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4/(c5*P + c6)
Candidate formulas: 57

GT (fixed) depends **only on P** (no t):
\[
f(P)=0.9198344660\,(1-\tfrac{P}{84.0283518631})P\;+\;0.9198344660\,\frac{P^2}{7.5314755755\,P+1}.
\]
Rewrite structure:
- Polynomial part: \(0.9198344660\,P - (0.9198344660/84.0283518631)\,P^2\) (so it has **P** and **P²** terms).
- Rational part: \(0.9198344660\,\dfrac{P^2}{7.5314755755 P+1}\) (a **P² over linear** term, with **nonzero** coefficient).

So any matching candidate must be expressible as
\[
aP + bP^2 + d\frac{P^2}{\alpha P + \beta}
\]
with \(d\neq 0\), and must be independent of \(t\) (or have all \(t\)-dependent parts forced to 0 by parameter choices).

---

### Candidates 1–8 (all terms share one linear denominator)
These are all of the form
\[
\frac{\text{(polynomial in P)}}{P c_1 + c_2}\quad \text{(or }Pc_1+1\text{)}.
\]
GT is **sum of a polynomial** \((aP+bP^2)\) **plus** a rational term \(\propto \frac{P^2}{7.531P+1}\), not a *single* rational function.

Could a single rational equal “polynomial + rational”? Only if, after bringing to common denominator, the numerator matches exactly. But GT has denominator \((7.531P+1)\) only on the rational part; the polynomial part is over 1. Writing GT over \((7.531P+1)\) gives:
\[
f(P)=\frac{(aP+bP^2)(7.531P+1)+dP^2}{7.531P+1}
\]
whose numerator includes a **\(P^3\)** term from \((aP+bP^2)(7.531P+1)\). So a single rational with denominator linear *could* in principle match if its numerator is cubic with the right coefficients.

However, candidates 1–8 have numerator constrained to specific combinations:
- They include only terms \(P^3, P^2, P\) (and sometimes constants) but **all divided by the same linear**.
- That seems promising, but GT’s denominator is specifically \(7.5314755755P+1\). We could set candidate denominator to that (choose \(c_1,c_2\) appropriately).
- The key issue: GT numerator over that denominator is **not arbitrary**; it is \((aP+bP^2)(7.531P+1)+dP^2\) which has **no constant term** and has a specific relationship among coefficients.

Let’s check if candidates can represent an arbitrary cubic numerator with no constant term:
- Candidate 1: \(\frac{c0 P^3 + (c3+c4)P^2 + (c5+c6)P}{Pc1+c2}\). Yes: cubic, quadratic, linear coefficients are freely adjustable (via c0, c3+c4, c5+c6), denominator adjustable (c1,c2). So it can match any target of that form.
- Candidate 2 similarly: \(\frac{c0 P^3 + (c2+c3)P^2 + (c4+c5)P}{P+c1}\) (denominator slope fixed to 1, but GT slope is 7.531..., so cannot match unless we allow scaling by rewriting—no, because denominator is exactly \(P+c1\), slope 1 fixed).
- Candidate 3/4/7 have denominator \(Pc1+1\) (intercept fixed 1, slope adjustable).
- Candidate 5/6/8 are like 1 but with extra redundant numerator parameters (still fine).

So the only plausible ones among 1–8 are those where we can set denominator to \(7.5314755755P+1\): that requires intercept 1 and slope 7.531..., i.e. forms \(Pc1+1\). That points to candidates **3,4,7** (and not 1/5/6/8 because their intercept is free but not fixed to 1; actually they *can* set intercept to 1 too, so 1/5/6/8 can also match the denominator exactly by choosing \(c2=1, c1=7.531...\)). So denominator matching is possible for 1,3,4,5,6,7,8.

But there is a deeper obstruction: GT is **not** a single fraction; but we already converted it to a single fraction over \((7.531P+1)\), so that’s not an obstruction. The real check is: does that single-fraction representation have the same functional form as candidate? Yes, it’s a cubic-over-linear with no constant term. Therefore candidates 1/3/4/5/6/7/8 *could* match if their numerator can be tuned to the exact cubic.

Let’s compute the implied cubic numerator coefficients for GT over \((kP+1)\) where \(k=7.5314755755\).
Let \(a=0.9198344660\), \(b=-(0.9198344660/84.0283518631)\), \(d=0.9198344660\).
Then
\[
\text{num}(P)=(aP+bP^2)(kP+1)+dP^2
= ak P^2 + aP + bk P^3 + bP^2 + dP^2.
\]
So coefficients:
- \(P^3\): \(bk\) (nonzero because \(b\neq 0\) and \(k\neq 0\))
- \(P^2\): \(ak + b + d\)
- \(P^1\): \(a\)
- constant: 0

Thus any candidate that can realize \(\frac{A P^3 + B P^2 + C P}{kP+1}\) can match by setting \(A=bk\), \(B=ak+b+d\), \(C=a\).

Now check each:

1. Candidate 1: \(\frac{c0 P^3 + (c3+c4)P^2 + (c5+c6)P}{Pc1+c2}\). Set \(c1=k\), \(c2=1\), \(c0=A\), choose \(c3,c4\) to sum to \(B\), choose \(c5,c6\) to sum to \(C\). Works.

2. Candidate 2: denominator \(P+c1\) slope fixed 1, cannot equal \(kP+1\) for all P unless \(k=1\). Not possible. So no.

3. Candidate 3: \(\frac{c0 P^3 + (c2+c3)P^2 + (c4+c5)P}{Pc1+1}\). Set \(c1=k\), \(c0=A\), \(c2+c3=B\), \(c4+c5=C\). Works.

4. Candidate 4: same as 3 but with extra \(P c6/(Pc1+1)\) i.e. linear coefficient becomes \(c4+c5+c6\). Still can set sum to \(C\). Works.

5. Candidate 5: like 1 but extra \(P c7\) term; linear coefficient becomes \(c5+c6+c7\). Still can match. Works.

6. Candidate 6: like 1 plus constants over denom \(c7/(...)+c8/(...)\) giving a **constant numerator term** \(c7+c8\). GT’s constant numerator term is 0, so set \(c7=-c8\) (or both 0). Works.

7. Candidate 7: like 3 plus constant over denom \(c7/(Pc1+1)\) giving constant numerator term \(c7\). Set \(c7=0\). Works.

8. Candidate 8: like 5 plus constants over denom \(c8+c9\). Set \(c8=-c9\). Works.

So **candidates 1,3,4,5,6,7,8 can be made exactly equal to GT for all P** (no special domain condition needed), by choosing parameters as above.

---

### Candidates 9–57
All of these include either:
- explicit **t-dependence** (sin, tanh, exp(t), log with t, etc.) that cannot be removed unless the whole term’s coefficient is set to 0, and/or
- rational terms of the wrong shape (e.g., \(P c2/(P c3 + c4)\) gives \(P/(linear)\), not \(P^2/(linear)\)), and/or
- missing the required \(P^2/(linear)\) term with nonzero coefficient.

Quick checks:
- 9,10,12,13–17,18–22,24–32,34–36,38–57: contain t-dependent terms; you can zero their coefficients, but then you’re left with at most a polynomial in P and/or \(P/(linear)\) and/or constants—none can produce the necessary \(P^2/(7.531P+1)\) term except those with an explicit \(P*c4/(P*c5+c6)\) etc., which is \(P/(linear)\), not \(P^2/(linear)\).
- 11,23,45: have \(P*c2/(P*c3+c4)\) and/or \(c6/(P*c3+c4)\): again \(P/(linear)\) and \(1/(linear)\), not \(P^2/(linear)\).
Thus none of 9–57 can match GT.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.9198(1 - P/84.028)P + 0.9198 \cdot P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

Let me expand this:
$$f(P) = 0.9198P - 0.9198P^2/84.028 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$
$$= 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

Note: The GT depends only on P, not on t. This is crucial.

Let me put everything over a common denominator $(7.531P + 1)$:
$$f(P) = \frac{0.9198P(7.531P + 1) - 0.01095P^2(7.531P + 1) + 0.9198P^2}{7.531P + 1}$$

Numerator:
- $0.9198P(7.531P+1) = 6.927P^2 + 0.9198P$
- $-0.01095P^2(7.531P+1) = -0.08246P^3 - 0.01095P^2$
- $+0.9198P^2$

Total numerator: $-0.08246P^3 + (6.927 - 0.01095 + 0.9198)P^2 + 0.9198P$
$= -0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P$

So GT = $\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531P + 1}$

This is a rational function of P with:
- Numerator: cubic in P (terms $P^3, P^2, P$, no constant)
- Denominator: linear in P $(c_1 P + 1)$

The GT has **no dependence on t**.

## Structural Requirements

The GT as a single fraction is: $\frac{aP^3 + bP^2 + cP}{dP + 1}$

This has 4 free parameters (a, b, c, d). Any candidate that can represent this form (with appropriate constants) matches.

Now let me check each candidate:

### Candidates 1-8: Rational functions with common denominator

**Candidate 1:** $\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_3+c_4)P^2 + (c_5+c_6)P}{c_1 P + c_2}$
This is $\frac{AP^3 + BP^2 + CP}{DP + E}$ — 5 effective parameters. This can match GT (which is $\frac{aP^3+bP^2+cP}{dP+e}$). ✓

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** $\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P}{P + c_1}$

Let me check: GT denominator is $7.531P + 1$. If we divide num and denom by 7.531, we get $\frac{num/7.531}{P + 1/7.531}$. The numerator would be $\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531}$. This is still $AP^3+BP^2+CP$ form. So yes, with $c_1 = 1/7.531$, this works. ✓

**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

Then $c_0 = -0.08246/7.531 = -0.01095$. $c_1 c_7 = c_1 = 0.9198$. $c_0 c_7 + c_1 c_6 = -0.01095 + 0.9198 \times 7.531 = -0.01095 + 6.927 = 6.916$. But GT needs $7.836$.
